The Writing Brush 222

— Sha Yongcai

The writing brush, known as the "three-inch hair cone," has a history of over 2,200 years since its invention by General Meng Tian of the Qin Dynasty.

The Vague Records of Imperial Incense 223

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

After I went inside to take a look, I immediately discovered many pieces of evidence: for example, the abundance of plaques dedicated to the gods, the cleanliness of the sweeping, and the splendor of the decorations, all of which were sufficient to show that the comical and laughable stories I perceived were indeed taken seriously by some people in the local area! They believed that thousands of years ago, there was indeed a fox with extraordinary powers who, because of his improper conduct, was punished by the Jade Emperor and specially descended to earth to cure all the sufferings of mankind, thereby repenting for his own sins. And because they had this belief, some people who fell ill actually got better after taking the "immortal remedy"!

The so-called Fox Immortal Pagoda was actually a very large temple, also with a very solemn and dignified atmosphere. In the main hall, there was also a very tall shrine, with two silk curtains embroidered with flowers hanging in front of the shrine, which should have been very bright and beautiful before, but now they have been stained old and dirty by incense smoke. In the middle of these two silk curtains, one could vaguely see a vermilion-lacquered golden-lettered spirit tablet inside, inscribed with nine regular script characters: "Spirit Tablet of the Imperial-Appointed Azure Fox Great Immortal." Below the shrine was an offering table, with candlesticks and incense burners, with red candles burning high and incense smoke lingering all day long, all supplied continuously by the devout men and women.

As for how the sick people came to seek treatment? This set of procedures is understood by nineteen out of ten Chinese people, and there were no special methods in the past. Just the same, a bamboo cylinder filled with bamboo sticks was held in the hands of the patient or their family members, first waved three times over the newly lit incense, as a sign of communicating with the gods, and then respectfully kowtowed, and slowly and carefully shook the stick cylinder. (209)

Although the writing brush is a small stationery item, it has already made a huge contribution to culture. The poets and men of letters of the Tang, Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties all used it to pass down their works for thousands of years, didn't they? If it weren't for it, what would they rely on to reveal their masterpieces to future generations?

The tools used by warriors are called weapons; the tools used by scholars are called stationery. Superficially, stationery cannot defeat weapons. However, in reality, this is not always the case. Take the pen as an example: the pen of a lawyer—commonly known as a "knife pen"—can often cause someone's death between numbers. This kind of bloodless killing can be said to be even worse than weapons.

Logically, since the writing brush has over two thousand years of culture and history, it should be further developed and expanded by now. However, the opposite is true. Now, its position in the hands of scholars is gradually being shaken. The steel pen, which is replacing its position, is slowly becoming the main guest, which is truly a very lamentable thing. If we examine the reasons for this, half of it is because the intellectual class is too fond of Westernization, and half of it is because the manufacturers are too conservative and do not make improvements.

Every day, seeing the large advertisements for "XX Fountain Pen Great Sales" in the newspapers, one cannot help but sigh for this "writing brush that has contributed so much to culture" and the "tens of thousands of craftsmen who rely on it for a living"!

Lucky and Unlucky 224

— Yue

Reading and Becoming an Official 225

— Ziwei

The greatest purpose of reading is "learning for application." Those who are illiterate and uneducated, if they want to "avoid being taken advantage of" in this era, unless they are rich in experience, can remedy their shortcomings, otherwise, they will inevitably fall into ruin.

However, the motives of the general public for reading are somewhat perverse, even eagerly wanting to become officials, hoping to climb out of the path of becoming an official, to make a fortune, to obtain honor, everything!

This is, of course, a fallacy.

Therefore, although the ancient proverb "excel in scholarship and then serve as an official, excel in serving as an official and then study" has its considerable reasons for existence, its application in the present is always somewhat inadequate. If reading is solely intended to achieve the goal of becoming an official, then the effect of education is inevitably too simple and too pitiful.

Regarding this similar issue, Wang Pingling once wrote a film script for "Bigamy," which was directed by the star Wu Cun into a film, and its powerful criticism is worthy of our attention.

Local Customs Anecdotes

Shanghai Colloquialisms in Shanghai Officialdom During the Tongzhi-Guangxu Period 226

— Shanghai Communication Society

In Shanghai, there are all kinds of people with all kinds of understandings. Then, let's talk about the Shanghai officialdom's observations of Shanghai during the Tongzhi-Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, which may be an interesting thing.

Chen Qiyuan, who served as the Shanghai County Magistrate as a descendant of the famous "Haining Family," said in his "Yongxian Zhai Notes":

"Since the Western powers opened trade in Shanghai, more than ten li outside the North Gate were designated for foreigners to reside in, and the foreigners paid rent for it annually, which is called the Concession. The Concession is divided among England, France, and three countries, and all public affairs are handled jointly by the Chinese-foreign Tongzhi and the consuls of the three countries. Local officials no longer participate in anything except for cases of murder and theft."

This is talking about the situation in the Concession. Although it is only a few simple sentences, he clearly stated that the opening of the Concession was after the opening of trade; he also knew very well that the opening of the port and the opening of the Concession could not be confused. During the Tongzhi-Guangxu period, the relationship between the Shanghai local officials and the legal rights of the Concession was exactly as he said, but at the time, the situation was extremely complex, and he was too fond of words and unwilling to say more.

Then, he wrote further, saying:

"The barbarians and Chinese are mixed together, the population is vast and numerous, and wealthy merchants and wandering people from all directions gather together. Brothels and妓館(prostitution houses) gather like the wind, residing in rows of houses, relying on foreigners as protectors, and the officials dare not scold them, and the authorities cannot question them, and they are becoming more and more prosperous, almost to the point of 花天酒地 (debauchery). When I was in charge of county affairs, I wanted to curb them slightly, but I was unable to do so, and I once ordered the local security guards in the foreign concession to secretly investigate them. Those with names numbered more than 1,500 houses, and 花烟館 (opium dens) and saltwater妹 (prostitutes from Hong Kong/Macau) and freshwater妹 (local prostitutes) were not included."

According to the above, since the mingling of Chinese and foreigners in the Concession in 1853 (the third year of Xianfeng), about twenty years had passed by the time Chen Qiyuan became the Shanghai County Magistrate in 1871 (the tenth year of Tongzhi), and there were already more than 1,500 brothels alone, not including others, and its deformed prosperity had undoubtedly become concrete.

He then narrated:

"Prostitution is prevalent, already surpassing the world. Since the Tongzhi era, foreign prostitutes have also come across the sea, flaunting their coquettishness, flirting with their eyes, in order to divide the profits of Chinese prostitutes. Thus, Chinese and foreigners are one family. Gentlemen from near and far, fond of pleasure-seeking, all choose the foreign settlement as their preferred place for amusement. The foreigners' harvesting of China's wealth can be said to have reached every extreme."

Originally, the arrival of Western prostitutes in Shanghai was during the Tongzhi era. His sentence "Chinese and foreigners are one family" was indeed humorous, as the literati of the time called it.

Others, there was Yu Benyu, a native of Xiuning, Anhui, who served as the Director-General of the Zhejiang Maritime Transport Bureau in Shanghai, and belonged to the ranks of alternate Daotais. In his "Record of a Visit to the Western Gardens," he wrote about Hongkou and the British Concession. Although it is archaic writing, the silhouette of the Shanghai Concession at the time, the so-called "scenery of the foreign settlement," can still be imagined. The following is an excerpt:

"In the first month of Yihai (according to the lunar calendar, i.e., the first month of Guangxu), without

ten days of sunshine, occasionally the weather cleared, but I still had to work on the riverfront, so I was still unaware of the passage of time. Long Kaichen Sima came from Anhui in the spring and temporarily resided at the Bureau. The Bureau is located outside the south gate of the city, and it is quite cramped. Shen Chen always thought of traveling north, because the essence of Shanghai is gathered here, and those who come from afar all yearn for it. ····· I, along with Qingyun, Anhui Sheng, and pulled Kaichen, the Li Pavilion, shared a sedan chair to Lao Zha. ··· Each left their sedan chair and rode in a horse-drawn carriage, letting go of the reins to travel. About ten miles, we arrived at the Hongkou Grain Storage Depot. (According to the Haikou Transportation Bureau's affiliate office) The three-room building was built along the river, and the sound of wheelboats and barges was heard in the harbor, which was not worth lingering over. So we boarded the carriage again. . . westward, from then on, it was a plain with gardens and willows. ··· Looking far away at the Chun Shen River, white boats and black awnings were as chaotic as flying birds. On the streets, the dust from carriages and horses, Chinese and foreigners, was mixed and chaotic, and lightning flashed and stars raced. Kaichen, having never seen such a sight before, couldn't help but clap his hands and exclaim. Suddenly, at a place where green trees surrounded a bay, the carriage stopped, and we saw everyone standing on the grass. At that time, fragrant carriages, precious horses, brocade clusters, and flower groups were everywhere. ··· There was a square well by the roadside, and there was also the ancient Jing'an Temple, but we did not visit it because of the detour. (The following omits the description of visiting the garden)"

Education News

Preparation for the Chinese Art Exhibition in London 242

Selecting Exhibits in Progress

A Preview to Be Held in Shanghai Next Spring

Regarding the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London, after the Executive Yuan decided to establish a Preparatory Committee, with the Minister of Education as the Chairman, the Deputy Ministers of the Ministries of Interior, Foreign Affairs, Finance, and Education as Standing Committee Members, and Chen Shuren, Zhang Daofan, etc. as Committee Members, it has been actively proceeding. On the British side, Lord Lytton was invited to be the Chairman of the Executive Committee. The central diplomatic authorities of the two countries recently formally expressed mutual agreement, stating that the meeting would be held under the joint supervision of the two governments. Regarding the scope and selection of exhibits, our country's Preparatory Committee has organized a special committee, with Ye Gongchuo, Zhu Wenjun, Guo Baochang, Xu Beihong, Gao Jianfu, Li Ji, Tang Lan, Rong Geng, Chen Handi, Deng Yizhe, etc. as Committee Members, and Yang Zhensheng as the Director of the Special Committee. It is reported that the Committee Members in Peiping will first draft a preliminary selection catalog of the antiquities in the Palace Museum and the Antiquities Exhibition Hall, and will meet with the Southern Committee Members in Shanghai in February next year to examine the actual objects and make the final selection of exhibits. The main categories of exhibits are calligraphy, painting, ceramics, and bronzes, each based on historical development, for a systematic exhibition. Other art products, such as jade, statues, wood carvings, embroidery, and lacquer, etc., will be selected for their quality and, to the extent possible, will also be systematically exhibited. In addition to selecting from the Palace Museum and the Antiquities Exhibition Hall, it is also planned to solicit works of art or antiquities from the Academia Sinica, the Central Museum, the Historical Museum, the Northwest Scientific Expedition, the Henan Museum, the Peiping Library, the Shandong and Anhui Provincial Libraries, Peking University, Yenching University, and private collections, in order to present the entire spectrum of Chinese art.

In order to show the credibility of this exhibition, in addition to printing and publishing the catalog and photos of the exhibits at the time of departure, it is also scheduled to hold a preview exhibition in Shanghai before shipping to England in March next year. After the items return to China, they will be exhibited once again in Nanjing. The above decisions have been successively approved by the Preparatory Committee, the Council of the Palace Museum, and the Executive Yuan. During the preview period, the British side will send five selection committee members to China to work with the Chinese experts to make the final selection. However, China will still reserve specially important items and will not allow them to be exhibited abroad.

Regarding the safety of the exhibits, after the final selection of items, the Chinese and British committee members will supervise the packaging by expert experts, and both parties will sign and seal them, and then they will be unsealed by both parties under supervision during the London exhibition. In addition to implementing various practical protective measures during transportation, the most important one will be that the British Navy Department will send warships to escort the goods from Shanghai to Singapore, and then escort them back from Singapore to Shanghai. During transportation, loading and unloading, and during the exhibition in England, the Preparatory Committee will send special personnel and competent guards to supervise and protect them at all times together with the British personnel in order to ensure thoroughness.

It is said that this exhibition will be an unprecedented international art exhibition in China. It is expected that it will enable international people to gain the most profound and universal understanding of the artistic creativity of the Chinese nation. Moreover, the holding of this exhibition is in response to the request of the British people to commemorate the 25th anniversary of the British Emperor's accession to the throne, which will surely benefit the friendly relations between China and Britain.

Education in War Zones Nears Bankruptcy 243

More Than 100,000 Children Out of School

Girls' Normal School Closed, Boys' Normal School Teaching on Borrowed Land

– Security Teams Occupy the Education Bureau and Schools –

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) Education in war zones is on the verge of bankruptcy, with over 100,000 children out of school. Yutian County is particularly affected. This reporter interviewed a certain gentleman from the educational circles of Yutian who came to Beiping. According to him, before the incident, Yutian County had two normal schools for men and women, nine higher primary schools, and over 300 lower primary schools. Recently, the Education Bureau, the Public Education Center, and the First Higher Primary School, among other schools, have been occupied by security teams. Moreover, due to the unrest in the area, only the Boys' Normal School is勉强勉强 able to hold classes on borrowed land, with only twenty-two students. The Girls' Normal School has long been closed. Only three or four higher primary schools, including Ya Hong Qiao, Ding Jia Qiao, and Zhu Shu Wu, are勉强勉强 holding classes. No more than forty or fifty lower primary schools are open. The number of children out of school is countless. The reason schools cannot open is entirely due to financial difficulties and disruption by the security teams. Many middle-class families have moved to other places. It is estimated that over 1,500 households have fled to Beiping, over 700 to Tianjin, over 200 to Tangshan, and countless others to Lu Tai and other places. The whole city is in a miserable state, indescribable. Although some people have stepped forward to provide relief, their efforts are too weak to make a difference.

Qi Lu University Students Petition Again 244

Student Roster Unable to Be Submitted to the Ministry Due to Unresolved University President Issue

– Education Director He Siyuan Promises to Petition the Ministry of Education Again –

(Quick Dispatch from Jinan) The issue of the president of the private Qi Lu University in Jinan has been unresolved for a long time, affecting the student roster, which has not been submitted to the Ministry of Education for record. To this day, the board of directors held a full meeting on the 5th of this month. Although Mei Yi Bao has been publicly recommended as president, Mei has been unable to come to Shandong recently and has not indicated whether he will take office. Chairman Kong Xiangxi has also not sent a telegram to Jinan. All the students' requests, the most important of which is the submission of the roster to the Ministry, have not been addressed. The students of the College of Liberal Arts and Sciences of the university believe that the long-standing unresolved issue of the president and the inability to submit the student roster to the Ministry greatly affect their studies and the future of the university. Therefore, they publicly elected Yang Xuexian, Li Fengge, Ma Lin, and others as representatives to visit Vice Chairman Li Zhifan at his residence on Wei Er Road at 3:00 PM today (the 22nd). Li was unavailable due to other matters. The representatives then went to the Education Department to see Director He Siyuan. He personally received them. The representatives stated their purpose and asked He if the student roster had been submitted to the Ministry. He replied that he had petitioned the Ministry of Education, but it was rejected because there was no official president. The representatives then requested He to appoint the university president from the Department to avoid prolonged disruption of university affairs, so that the roster could be submitted to the Ministry as soon as possible, so as not to affect the students' future. He said that this would have to be petitioned to the Ministry of Education before it could be handled. The representatives then left and returned to the university. It is also heard that Li Zhifan recently received a private letter from Mei Yi Bao, which stated that Mei had not yet severed ties with Yenching University and that he would need to consider whether to take the position of president of Qi Lu University before making a decision.

The Central Government Has Not Yet Issued a Clear Order for the Implementation Plan of the National Children's Year 250

The City's Children's Year Preparatory Committee Held an Emergency Meeting Yesterday

Decided to Postpone the Opening Ceremony on New Year's Day, Etc.

The Full-Year Children's Program Will Still Be Held According to the Original Proposal

Since the National Government decided that next year will be China's Children's Year, the city's party and government organs have organized a Children's Year Preparatory Committee to be responsible for the preparations and have scheduled an opening celebration ceremony for Children's Year to be held at the City Hall on New Year's Day. They have also decided on a full-year children's program. All of this has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the City's National Children's Year Preparatory Committee, in light of the fact that the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education have not yet made a concrete decision on the implementation plan for the National Children's Year, believes that if Shanghai proceeds independently, it would be no different from Shanghai's Children's Year alone. Therefore, they convened an emergency meeting at the City Government yesterday to make a definite resolution. Those who attended were Li Dachao, Pan Gongzhan (representing Hu Shuyi), Li Tingan (representing Hu Jingxiu), Hu Shuyi, Wang Guanyi, and Qian Fugong as an observer. Li Dachao chaired the meeting, and Qian Fugong took the minutes. First, Committee Member Hu reported that although the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education were responsible for preparing for the National Children's Year, the National Government had not yet issued a clear order. If Shanghai were to proceed independently, it would be no different from this year's Shanghai Children's Year. Therefore, a definite resolution must be made at this meeting on how to proceed. The discussion then began: (1) Should the city's opening ceremony continue to be prepared, given that the National Children's Year has not yet been promulgated by the National Government? It was resolved that before the National Government issues a clear order, in addition to the full-year children's program continuing to be carried out by the responsible agencies and organizations according to the resolution of the first meeting, the opening ceremony and New Year's Day events will all be held in accordance with the national schedule after the central government issues a clear order. (2) Should the city government be requested to forward a request to the National Government to promulgate next year as the National Children's Year as soon as possible? It was resolved to be handled by the Children's Welfare Association. (3) Given that the opening ceremony has been temporarily suspended, should the special issues of the various newspapers be published as planned? It was resolved that materials should continue to be collected as usual and that all newspapers should be notified to publish them simultaneously with other parts of the country. The meeting was then adjourned.

Dental Expert Su Jielang Passes Away 256

Chen Xiaodie and Others Initiate a Memorial Service

Su Jielang, Director of the Children's Dental Hospital, was a well-known dental expert in the country. He was 26 years old and from Xiamen. He graduated from the Tokyo Dental College in the 20th year of the Republic of China. After graduating, he stayed in the hospital for research. Later, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau entrusted the embassy in Japan to recruit specialized dental personnel from Japan. Ambassador Jiang Zuobin introduced him to Shanghai, where he served as a technician in the Municipal Health Bureau and as the Director of the Dental Department of the Shanghai Health Education Committee and a health committee member of the Children's Welfare Association. Later, he resigned from the Health Bureau and served as the Director of the Shanghai Children's Dental Hospital, which is owned by the Home Industry Company. The hospital's operations became increasingly prosperous, all thanks to Su's efforts. Su was honest and diligent in his work. Unfortunately, he contracted typhoid fever last month and passed away at 7:00 PM on the 23rd of this month. A coffin was placed at the Quanzhang Guild Hall at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. It is heard that Su's friends Chen Xiaodie, Li Xingfu, Wu Liyuan, Yin Wujuan, Zhou Shang, Hu Shuyi, and others are preparing to initiate a memorial service.

Page 14

Free Talk

On the Usefulness of "Scholars" 261

— Meng Jia

Mr. Cao Juren lamented the "utter uselessness" of scholars. Although this statement seems to be very worldly-wise, in reality, it is not so. Emperor Xuan of Han did not use scholars because a "vulgar Confucian was out of touch with the times, favoring the ancient over the present, causing people to be confused by names and realities, and not knowing what to adhere to." The reason why Old Master Ni in "The Scholars" had to sell his last son, having been a poor scholar for thirty-seven years, was precisely because he "had read a few dead books and could not handle light or bear heavy burdens."

In fact, vulgar Confucians are not all "out of touch with the times." Such Confucians are truly "vulgar" through and through. There have been many non-"vulgar" Confucians in history. And it is precisely because of this that these refined scholars have become "useful."

Huang Zhongze perhaps had the lament "utter uselessness is a scholar" because he was "unappreciated." The reason why Old Master Ni was "useless" was precisely because, although he "couldn't even keep the youngest child," he could only complain to the actor Bao Wenqing and never had any thought of resistance.

Scholars are not "useless," but their "usefulness" is different.

Wearing a silk turban and holding a feather fan, simply preserving elegance; drinking bitter tea, playing with antiques, and hiding in a study to talk about foxes and ghosts, is just "helpless," isn't it? Doubt, depression, and sadness are precisely the characteristics of the dark side of a transition period. The remnants in the cauldron of the times, whether they are groaning or paralyzed in silence, are still just remnants. However, this attitude toward life is still a kind of "usefulness" because, objectively, it helps maintain the old era.

However, modern scholars are not limited to this. "Taking off their long gowns," they are no longer scholars in essence. Daring to gaze at reality, they understand: "Sorrow and pain we will surely have, and struggle will certainly be endless. We must combine courage and pain into one and carve out a path from constant struggle." They sing the lines of Yesenin's poem: "Death is not difficult, the difficulty lies in how to rebuild life," and throw themselves into the struggle for light. Such scholars can be said to be the "new type" of scholars; they are no longer the famous scholars burning incense and sipping tea in the Bitter Rain Studio.

Scholars are not "useless," but their "usefulness" is different, and therefore their value is also different.

Homecoming 262

— Hei Ying

The day I left this place, as usual, I got up at dawn. Barefoot and sturdy, I carried a tin bucket to the back of the house to shower. A-Man was a little sentimental today; although he was already twenty years old, it was his first time leaving home. He thought about how he would soon be far away in Singapore - what a resounding metropolis! There, he would be in contact with many strangers; he would be working all day in that shop by the coast, and that mischievous Lina would no longer be able to be with him every day.

(When will I be back after leaving?")

He asked himself that.

In the early morning, a cool breeze blew behind the house. The sun was still playing hide-and-seek, not yet climbing up. A rooster's crow woke up Lina next door.

They met by a coconut tree.

A-Man, leaning against the trunk of the tree, was also bare-chested. His strong physique often made women sing hymns of praise in their hearts. He put the bucket on the ground, his eyes fixed on her face. She seemed even more beautiful, with a lovely blush on her cheeks. He suddenly hugged her, shouting:

"Lina! I really don't want to go to Singapore!"

"What? Are you crazy? Your father is sending you there to make a fortune. A-Man, you haven't been there yet, it's really fun. You can walk on the road for half a day, looking at many new things and not wanting to eat. It's even more interesting at night. It's just that there are a lot of bad women... You have to be careful thinking of me..."

Her voice suddenly lowered as she said this. The first ray of sunlight shone up, illuminating her face as she lowered her head. A-Man raised her pointed chin with his hand; suddenly he noticed two lines of clear tears hanging on her face, which had previously been flushed with a lovely blush...

"Lina, are you crying?"

"·····"

She didn't answer, just shook her head.

"Why are you crying? I am... Didn't Hei Ying

say I'm going to make a fortune? You wait for me for two or three years, I will definitely come back. Come back and you..."

"But..."

"But what? Lina, tell me!"

Lina didn't say anything; the sound of calling A-Man was already ringing in the house. He threw her down and ran in. His father was putting on his clothes, and said to him:

"The train leaves at nine o'clock, we're leaving soon."

"Okay."

He planned to change into a clean suit and take the hat out of the closet. His father muttered to him:

"A-Man, you're not young anymore. You have to know that our family is poor, even your mother has to go to other people's houses to be a nanny. You go to Singapore, work hard, save some money and bring it back..."

"I'll listen to you, don't worry."

"Are you ready? We're leaving."

"Let's go."

So, the father went ahead, and A-Man came out carrying a big bundle. The sun was already high in the sky, and there were voices everywhere. Turning his head occasionally, he saw Lina waving to him at the door of the next house...

A month later, at noon, the tropical sun was steaming on people's heads as usual. It was still that bundle, that face, although a little thinner. A-Man jumped off the train and went straight home. Sweat streamed down his back, soaking his white linen coat. His steps were limping, appearing a bit heavy. Some people by the road recognized him, saying:

"That's A-Man. Did he make a fortune, coming back so quickly."

However, in A-Man's ears now, it was simply full of sarcasm. He hissed uncomfortably, and felt his pocket, leaving only about one dollar. The closer he got to home, the more he lost courage; when he saw his father, how should he tell him?

His father was hoping he would save some money and come back!

However, he didn't know how Singapore had changed. Unemployment, theft, suicide, trouble... The peace he had when he worked in a foreign firm there five years ago had long become history.

Could A-Man, a Malay who didn't understand the ways of the world and grew up in the countryside, stand his ground in Singapore - a metropolis where economic panic had become acute?

So he came back...

He was familiar with the sandy road leading directly to his home. He was also familiar with the weeds by the road. He saw his own broken house from afar, with a coconut tree behind the house. The house on the left was Lina's: thinking of her, a smile appeared on the dusty corner of his mouth.

He pushed open the door with one hand and shouted:

"Dad!"

But there was no response. He put down the bundle and looked around in all directions, but there was no trace of his father. He thought, he probably went outside. So he ran to Lina's house.

"Lina!"

There was no response either.

Lina's mother came out. He grabbed her and asked:

"Do you know where my father went?"

"I'm afraid he went to the plantation."

"Where's Lina?"

"When did you come back?"

Hearing the woman in the sarong answering irrelevantly, A-Man was very anxious and widened his eyes, saying:

"Just came back. Where did Lina go?"

"Lina? That's right, you're asking about my daughter... She got married the day before yesterday."

"Married! Heavens..."

As if an arrow had hit his chest, he walked out. He didn't go back home, just walked aimlessly under the scorching sun. He didn't know who Lina had married; nor did he know where to go, always following this sandy road...

Cocoon (5) 263

— Original by Rin-yu Hayashi, Translated by Shizuko

We were sleeping on the grassy hill of a schoolyard spire overlooking an antique clock tower. The early summer sunlight glinted warmly from the new brass buttons, reflecting off our eyelids as we chatted idly. Suddenly, Sakai seemed to remember something.

"I still have those cocoons to deal with, don't I?"

"Ah, is your mother still working at the factory?"

"She won't quit, no matter what. She says, 'Until you graduate from school,' she'll keep working even if she has to chew on rocks." But in reality, it's hard for her to quit. Aside from working at the factory, there's no other way for my mother to live while I'm at school."

Sakai bit his lip, plucking at the grass on the hill. He spoke again, in a thoughtful tone.

"Lately, I've started to have doubts about this world. Take that factory, for example. There are still three hundred female workers working there. Most of them are girls from nearby farming villages, fifteen or sixteen to twenty-three or four years old. When they first arrive, they're young country girls with very strong bodies, but after a year or two, they return to the village with white cloths wrapped around their throats, or coughing, or with red eyes, or with festering fingers." Some even die in the factory like withered grass, and I've heard stories of girls whose hair got caught in the machines and crushed to death."

"The heavy, humid air and the ceaseless labor, the inadequate food—when I see those female workers whose young bodies are gradually being worn away, I think of the cocoons they're spinning in the boiling pots."

"Constantly being boiled, a thread so fine that the eye can't see it absorbs its life, gradually, gradually shrinking it, until soon it becomes a jet-black pupa—a useless corpse—floating on the surface of the boiling water."

"But on the other hand, if you look closely—aren't there people who are fattening themselves by sucking the life out of the cocoons, just like the spinning bobbins whirring above their heads?"

Sakai paused briefly, wiping the sweat from his forehead, and then said in a low voice:

"When I think about it—it's terrible—my mother probably won't be able to work safely in that factory until I graduate from university. For my mother, it's almost become a belief. She always thinks that it's her responsibility that the Sakai family declined, and she wants to make sure it can be revived no matter what. Not only that, but my mother undoubtedly feels a strong joy and a will to strive in educating me, her only son. I know that feeling... I know it very well."

"But if my mother is in that factory, isn't she just another one of those poor silkworms? An invisible thread is sucking away her life..."

I didn't know how to answer him.

A third-year student at a higher school—a winter day nearing graduation.

Late at night, Sakai braved the snow to come to my apartment.

"What is it?"

When I saw his bloodless face, like someone who had run out of a graveyard, I had an immediate, ominous premonition.

"My mother is dead! ...Too late!"

As I snatched the telegram he held out, I thought of the words he had predicted in the past, and a chill ran down my spine.

"Ah!?"

I didn't say anything. The quiet, old-fashioned eyebrows that I had seen in the room where the silk threads were turning in the silk mill immediately came to mind, but then immediately vanished.

"Too late! During the New Year's holiday, I begged my mother to let me suspend my studies no matter what. I begged her like that, saying, 'If I don't get you out of the factory, not only will I, as your son, be unable to bear it, but I feel an imminent and unavoidable danger, and I really can't rest easy.' When I returned home after a long absence, I could clearly see the deterioration of my mother's health. But my mother always cried and wouldn't listen."

He bit his lip, wiping away the tears that flowed.

But it's no use saying anything now. I have to go back tonight. I'm very sorry, but please lend me some travel expenses."

"Okay!"

I took out all the money I had and, treading through the snow, saw him off at the station.

On a Boat 264

— Yang Cheng

Under the tangent formed by the square roof of the pier and the circle of the large building behind, the shadows of a group of friends were receding, receding, and finally disappeared into the evening mist.

The sky gradually sank. After wiping away the lingering tears, I sighed sadly and looked with longing eyes towards Guangzhou, which was already beyond the line of sight.

Downstream of the Pearl River, the boat sailed peacefully on the wide river channel, the muddy yellow water lapping against the hull, as if whispering. The banks were low dikes, covered with lychee and longan groves, with small farmhouses occasionally appearing in the dense gaps; wisps of smoke curling up. Farther away, vast rice fields stretched out, cut off by dark hills.

Year after year, I wandered with the heart of a vagabond, running around everywhere. When I felt tired of the city, I resolutely left, like a Gypsy, going from one place to another. I fell asleep as soon as I lay down. When I woke up, I had already arrived in Hong Kong, and the night view from the top of Victoria Peak was a little tired. The salty, fishy Hong Kong market slept silently. I borrowed a hotel room to stay in, taking advantage of the Asian Queen's northward voyage the day after tomorrow.

Once the boat left Lei Yue Mun, it was a blue sky and a blue sea, with clouds and sea connecting at the horizon. The passengers in the third-class cabin endured the heat emanating from the nearby engine room, barely able to breathe, the air congealing like a solid, hard block. People's minds were muddled, stinging, unable to sleep. Occasionally, jazz music leaked out from the first-class cabin, but it wasn't needed here. Our tiny hope was a little breeze.

This golden yuan nation's ship, everything is like this society, full of obvious contradictions, why does the first-class cabin have such extravagance and comfort, but in the third-class cabin, not even a little breeze can be obtained, this is a mystery; the mystery of the imperialists.

After pleading and begging, the yellow-faced compatriots on the crew finally used their benevolent grace, so we had three wind funnels. Here is a microcosm of Chinese society, with various gambling and Cantonese food, but spreading among this group are deception and selfishness.

Time is quiet in the late night, the yellow light soaking some travel sorrows, some loneliness, then lingering in the traveler's heart, making meager dreams, the place to arrive tomorrow should be a place of freedom.

Returning from the Volcano (5) 265

— Lan Ru

Go! Even if you have only your last breath left, you must struggle to reach the volcano! Do not fear difficulties. No matter how difficult and dangerous the road ahead may be, you must desperately move forward. This is the best lesson for you in how to live your life. If you can reach the volcano, it will be like creating fresh and vibrant life in a desert-like existence in the future. The road of life is even more dangerous and difficult to walk than this. But if you risk your life to go—yes, you must have such aspirations, even if I die halfway before reaching my destination, I must move forward!—you will eventually reach your goal one day.

Go! Even if you have only your last breath left, you should move towards your destination.

With great difficulty, I mustered up the courage to approach Mr. Qin in one breath. He said unhappily, "You are walking too slowly. (There is another Little Yang who is as behind as I am.) Look, people have already returned from the volcano. Hurry up and leave, or you won't be able to catch the boat." At that time, I really wanted to say, "If we can't catch it, let's stay another night." But I was afraid of being scolded, and it was also impossible in reality, so I had no choice but to continue walking without daring to stop for even a second.

Suddenly, my left ear screamed a few times, and I saw stars before my eyes. I fainted on the sand.

"Hurry up and leave, don't rest."

Mr. Qin unceremoniously hit me on the back with a stick, which made me almost want to yell out.

"I'm not resting, I really can't walk anymore!"

"Why can others walk, but you can't?"

He actually started dragging me with his hands, and like dragging an object, without considering that I was a sentient being. In order to avoid being dragged and beaten by him, I had no choice but to grit my teeth and drag my legs, which weighed a thousand pounds, towards the volcano.

When teams of men and women returning from the volcano passed by me, seeing the many bright red bloodstains on their dark faces, I thought to myself that it was really not easy to go to the volcano once. Have I not suffered enough, and do I still have to bleed?

As a result, this month was slightly better by 2.5 li, January was better by 1 fen, February was better by 1 fen and 2.5 li, March was better by 1 fen and 7.5 li, April was better by 2 fen and 2.5 li, and May was better by 2 fen and 7.5 li.

Futures Wheat Was Brought Up By Flour In The Afternoon 278

Yesterday's futures wheat market, after the opening in the morning, each month showed a clear and stagnant appearance. Although the quotation for foreign wheat was better by about 1-2 jiao, due to the near closing, both inside and outside the industry were mostly collecting, so the transaction was sparse when the opening price was opened, and the price did not change. Until the afternoon opening, it was still hovering at first, and the price was also stable. At the closing, the market was slightly better due to the firm flour market, but the transaction was still light. As a result, this month was better by 1 fen, January was better by 2 fen, February was better by 1 fen, March was better by 3 fen, and the high-quality spot wheat rebounded by 1-2 fen. The medium and lower grades were flat. As for the factory's purchase, it was still active. The opening price for Guide wheat was 4 yuan and 5 fen, the second grade was 0.03 yuan, Yaowan wheat was 4 yuan and 3 fen, the second grade was 4 yuan, Luohe wheat was 4 yuan, the second grade was 3 yuan and 9 jiao and a half, Hankou wheat was 3 yuan and 8 jiao and 2 fen, the second grade was 7 jiao and 9 fen. It is estimated that Fufeng purchased 8,000 bags, Shenda purchased 3,000 bags, and Huafeng purchased 1,000 bags.

Chicago wheat bulls took profits sporadically, making it difficult to rise. Judging from this situation, the trend of rise and fall is indistinguishable, and will shift depending on the foreign market. Last week, the supply decreased by 2.933 million bushels. As for corn, due to the weather conditions, it is expected to promote the need for fodder and hinder the transportation of crops. Inferior Saigon Opened Down 10 Yuan 280

Price Reduction Transactions and Recovery of Prosperity

Yesterday, the arrival and storage of customer Xian rice were both thin, and the market stabilized. The price of foreign rice was slightly higher by 5 fen due to the desire of the merchants to sell. The prices were all slightly lower by 5 fen. In the afternoon, Shan Da Cheng sold 10,000 bags of Saigon 60-grain broken rice No. 2 inferior Saigon, and the price dropped to 10 yuan. The arrival and sales of customer Xian rice were both small yesterday. The inland successively handled 1,500 bags, Beiyang handled 250 bags of red rice, and the main street handled 220 bags of Yuan rice. The other bags were not sold, and the market price did not rise or fall.

Silk and Tea: A Review of the Local Silk Market 282

In recent days, the silk market has not seen much trading due to the upcoming Christmas and New Year holidays for Western merchants. Most of the exported goods this time are goods that were sold off earlier. This year, the silk market has seen a sharp decline in prices, resulting in a sharp reduction in transactions. The total export volume has decreased by 47% compared to last year, and one-tenth of that in 1926. The silk industry has always been the main foreign trade of our country. Since 1930, it has been declining, and in the past two years, it has plummeted. The impact on urban prosperity and rural economy is truly unimaginable. I hope that the authorities and the financial community will not take this serious problem lightly. The following is a comparison of the total export volume of raw silk in the past year and this year (although this year has not ended, it is not difficult to know the overall situation by reading this table).

Soviet Tea Production Increases Sharply 283

Soviet Russia has always been the only consumer country of Chinese tea. Since the country has implemented the Five-Year Plan twice, it has made unremitting efforts to promote tea. According to news from Russia, the country's tea production this year is 12.5 million pounds, an increase of 40% over last year. Most of it is used for machine-made Gongxi and brick tea. It is expected that tea will be self-sufficient in three or four years. In the future, China's tea trade with Russia is likely to gradually decline.

Sugar Market: Domestic Green Sugar Shows Signs of Loosening 284

Yesterday's sugar market showed a firm trend. The association's price list was 18 yuan and 7 jiao for ordinary spot crude white sugar, 18 yuan and 8 jiao for local goods, 5 yuan and 2 jiao and a half for transshipment goods, 14 yuan for ordinary 8-9 grade Dutch red sugar, 14 yuan and 7 jiao and 8 fen for high 10 grade, 18 yuan for No. 1 fine white sugar from local factory, and Chao Bang opened more than 300 bags of new Chao green sugar, with prices ranging from 11 yuan and 8 jiao to 11 yuan and 2 jiao. The trend was flat and tired, and the sales channels are inevitably slightly sluggish as the Gregorian New Year approaches, and the market has a tendency to continue to loosen. Although the number of new Diao green arrivals is small, it is difficult to exclusively occupy a good position due to the squeezing of Chao green sugar.

Supplementary Edition of the *Shen Bao* in this Locality

Talk

The 50 Million Yuan Theft Case 299

— Blowing

A small thief steals something worth dozens of copper coins, and he will be taken to the authorities. He will be detained for a month at most, and a week at least, before being released. In the past, although there was no death penalty for theft, if the value of the stolen goods exceeded one thousand yuan, the thief should be beheaded.

During the reign of Emperor Wen of the Han dynasty, someone stole a jade ring from in front of the seat in the Gao Temple. When the thief was caught, the court officials tried him and reported that he should be executed and his body left exposed in the marketplace. Execution meant killing him. Emperor Wen was furious and said, "This man is unprincipled and stole the late emperor's belongings. I wanted to punish his whole family, but you are trying him according to the law. This is not how I intend to jointly inherit the ancestral temple." The thief had only stolen a jade ring from the Gao Temple, but Emperor Wen felt that sentencing him to death was not enough. He was determined to exterminate his entire family before he would be satisfied.

Now, Yi Peiji has stolen treasures from the Forbidden City worth over 50 million yuan. The treasures of the Forbidden City are the treasures of our country. Yi Peiji, as the director of the Palace Museum, embezzled the treasures, amounting to a huge sum of 50 million yuan. Even if Yi Peiji were a judge, how should he sentence himself?

Yet Yi Peiji himself forgot that he was a great thief of the nation, and even boasted to his wives and concubines, allowing his wife to flaunt the stolen treasures, parading them in large banquets. (According to reports, the discovery of this huge case of treasure theft and fraud was due to Ms. Cui Zhenhua, who noticed that the jewelry, hairpins, and fox fur coats worn by Yi Peiji's wife at a certain banquet were rare treasures in society. Therefore, she became suspicious and investigated, which led to the cracking of such a major treasure theft case.) Yi Peiji, as a great thief, forgot that he was a thief, and his wife, wearing the stolen goods, forgot that they were stolen and dared to wear them openly in public. If they were not insane, how could they disregard the law and treat punishments with such contempt?

Only by believing in the promise of reward and the certainty of punishment, according to national law, if Yi Peiji, who embezzled treasures while being in charge of them, is not arrested and severely punished, how can it serve as a warning to other thieves in the world? It is rumored that Yi fears arrest and has fled to the Northeast, which is a possible reality. Although the Northeast is a place to hide dirt and accommodate filth, Yi Peiji stole national treasures, and his character is not only bankrupt but has also been sentenced to death long ago. Although some people may be tempted by his wealth and temporarily harbor him, they will never trust him fundamentally. The government should make every effort to arrest him and bring him to justice, so as to appease the public and intimidate thieves.

Believers 300

— Yonghui

The child's mouth was slightly open, and air was only coming out, not going in. He had been wearing the "hundred family garment" for three days. It was said that the hundred family garment could ward off evil, but for some reason, the child's illness grew more serious day by day, and even the hundred family garment lost its power to ward off evil.

"The Bodhisattva Guanyin who saves from suffering and delivers from difficulty, please save my child," the mother said, pressing her hands together in front of her chest and kneeling on both knees on a stool. She silently chanted, her complexion not as stiff as before, now appearing unusually kind and pitiful. Tears fell from her eyelids as she moved them slightly. "As long as the Bodhisattva can ensure my child's recovery, I will eat vegetarian food for the rest of my life and become a nun if necessary."

"I'll pray to Guanyin Niangniang for you again, no need to cry," Sister-in-law Shan, not knowing when, had strolled in, patting the widow's shoulder, showing sympathy and concern. "I'll get some incense ash from Guanyin Niangniang for you, and a yellow talisman, and I guarantee it will work as soon as you eat it! The Bodhisattva trusts me the most."

Sister-in-law Shan was a well-known good person in this village. If anyone wanted to pray to the gods or ask for divination, they always needed her. The villagers believed that her prayers and divination were more effective than anyone else's because she ate vegetarian food and was a disciple of Guanyin Niangniang. She herself said that Guanyin Niangniang had appeared to her in a dream and told her so in person. Moreover, her divination fee was very cheap, only 200 coins each time.

Incense ash and yellow talismans had been swallowed! The child's illness still did not improve.

"Sister-in-law Zhang, this can't go on. You should get a doctor to treat the child," several neighbors advised her.

The widow disagreed because she only had this one precious orphan. If he took the wrong medicine or if something went wrong, who would she rely on? She always believed that doctors could only diagnose minor ailments like stomach aches. More serious illnesses could only be cured by revering the Bodhisattva. Among the Bodhisattvas, none was more powerful or effective than Guanyin Niangniang. She had heard many stories from the *Journey to the West*. Even Sun Wukong with his great abilities could not do without the Guanyin of the South Sea, let alone her? In the past two years, she had truly become a worshiper of Guanyin.

The hundred family garment could not drive away the evil spirits, and the incense ash and yellow talismans had lost their effectiveness in saving lives. One early morning, the child silently bid farewell to his beloved mother and passed away.

A large crowd of neighbors stood in the widow's room, each offering words of comfort.

"Sister Zhang, please think of the deceased and don't cry."

"The person is already dead, crying is useless!"

"You should prepare for the funeral!"

"I knew long ago that this child couldn't be saved," Sister-in-law Shan said, frowning, her gray hair shining, and her pale face looking unusually serious. "Guanyin Niangniang gave me a dream the night before last, saying that this child came to collect a debt. His mother owed him a debt in a previous life. You see, once the debt was paid, he left! This was predetermined in a previous life, crying is useless. I knew long ago that he couldn't be raised." Sister-in-law Shan said, squeezing into the crowd at this time.

Pockmarked Chen San 301

— TT

Pockmarked Chen San has lost his job again. He sighs all day long, and his appetite is particularly bad. Compared to when he was a clerk at Rongchang Candle Shop, he eats almost a whole bowl less per meal. His face is also getting thinner, and his cheekbones are sticking out high, looking just like a monkey's face. His mother, Auntie Dalai, is also much more haggard because of his unemployment. On the one hand, she is worried about the rice in the rice jar, which is so shallow that she can see the bottom and can't fill it up. But what worries her most is her son Pockmarked Chen San's face, which is getting so thin that it's frightening. She went to the Fude Nunnery to pray to the Buddha and knelt before the Bodhisattvas in the City God Temple. From the fortune sticks given to her by the Buddha and Bodhisattvas, she carefully deduced that a benefactor would appear soon, so there was no need to worry. The Buddha and Bodhisattvas are all-powerful and most reliable. Their words can't be wrong, right? So she waited, waiting for the benefactor to descend.

But as the days passed, the benefactor didn't even show a shadow. Rice had been borrowed from the neighbors several times, and judging from the looks on their faces, it would be difficult to ask again.

Pockmarked Chen San is a little different from his mother. The sighs have gradually decreased, and he spends his days talking happily or going to the streets with his friends to watch plays. His appearance is completely different from before. Although he is still thin, he looks energetic.

Auntie Dalai is undoubtedly hoping that he can continue on this happy path and not ruin his health with worry. However, when she touches the rice in the rice jar, her heart turns cold. She feels that her son's idleness is not quite right. So she says:

"You should find something to do to earn money. It's not good to be idle all the time."

"Of course! But it's not easy to find a job!" Pockmarked Chen San has never spoken to his mother so sharply.

Auntie Dalai's face darkens, her nose feels sore, and she can't speak. Tears fall from the corners of her eyes.

In the past, when Pockmarked Chen San saw his mother so sad, he would surely comfort her, saying:

"There's no need to be like this. We'll slowly think of a solution."

But today, he takes his anger out on his mother and speaks sharply. With fire in his eyes, he rushes out the door.

Auntie Dalai watches her son's back. She thinks that her son's attitude has changed quickly, "He doesn't want to wear the short black cloth shirt he's worn for two or three years anymore, saying it's too ugly. He combs his hair so it shines, and it's fragrant and smooth. He plays all day long, regardless..." Auntie Dalai can't help but sob.

Pockmarked Chen San comes back in, followed by Mao Shi Di and a group of others. Pockmarked Chen San glances at them, and they walk in silently. The group gathers around the table and whispers together.

Auntie Dalai wants to find out about her son's recent activities. She deliberately walks past them, listening intently.

"Ah San, that young one is not bad, right? Her skin is so smooth," Mao Shi Di says to Pockmarked Chen San.

Pockmarked Chen San gives him a look, and the air immediately becomes silent again.

But the phrase "her skin is so smooth" rings especially loudly in Auntie Dalai's ears.

Page 18

Seeking the Truth Behind the Disappearance 302

— Zhu Li

In the morning, newspapers spread out from Wangping Street, reaching every reader through every road and alley.

On the second page of the social news section was a two-column-long news item about a marital dispute: the protagonist was the daughter of Manager Lu of the Shanghai ×× Factory.

According to the newspaper's report: Miss Lu was a high-achieving student at the ×× Girls' School, excelling in both character and academics, and highly regarded by the school's teachers and elders. Eighteen years ago, she was betrothed in the womb to the son of a colleague of Manager Lu, surnamed Zhu. Now that the wedding date had arrived, Miss Lu opposed this arranged marriage and therefore disappeared, so the report stated.

This sensational news became the first topic of conversation among friends that afternoon, just like during the Shanghai war. In teahouses and taverns, there were even more irresponsible propagandists spreading outlandish rumors.

The next morning, an advertisement appeared: "All matters can be resolved. Please return quickly after seeing this..."

Within the ×× Girls' School and the ×× Factory, there were naturally even more discussions, as if everyone was completely clear about the case, and visitors during these two days put aside their personal matters to first discuss this "morphine needle" news.

Thus, several days later, many so-called 100% accurate insider stories about the case were gathered, making it impossible to figure out the truth.

Half a month later, everyone became indifferent to the case, or it was replaced by newer news.

Three months later, those who were once very confident in their views no longer mentioned the case.

A year later, it was as if the case had never happened, and everything was calm.

But our Miss Lu has safely returned.

"All matters have been resolved."

As Miss Lu pretended to be sorrowful and threw herself into her mother's arms, Manager Lu hurriedly took out the divorce agreement from the locked dressing table drawer, and, while maintaining his fatherly dignity, said:

"Now that things are settled! But a girl shouldn't be so willful. It doesn't sound good to others! You should also think about your father's current position!"

After speaking, he stroked the short mustache on his lip, feeling very satisfied with how the matter was handled.

"Alright, our daughter has already returned, what more is there to say!"

The wife, while patting her daughter's shoulder, blamed her husband; she naturally had her own womanly reasoning.

Because of their daughter's disappearance, the old couple had several arguments. Manager Lu believed that his daughter was too inconsiderate of his position and reputation, doing such a shameful thing. As a father, he had plenty of money and could fix anything, but now everyone knew about it, which was disgraceful! The wife, after all, loved her daughter dearly, and at the age of fifty, this was her only darling daughter. She was also dissatisfied with her daughter's marriage. Back when they arranged the marriage in the womb, everyone was poor, but now her husband was a manager, and she should marry a son-in-law who was her equal.

"Relying on half a son!" This was the wife's reasoning.

The manager, on the other hand, didn't think about these things. His daughter would always belong to someone else's family. If the son-in-law had no money, he could give him one or two hundred thousand, and he wouldn't have to worry about food for life. The father had plenty of money! His mistress had already given birth to a son, but he couldn't bring him back, and his daughter had to do such an unseemly thing!

They argued and quarreled every day, and only after making the mistress's matter public as a condition was the daughter's divorce settled.

"All matters have been resolved."

Miss Lu secretly told her mother that she was already "that," that the future son-in-law was coming tomorrow to discuss the marriage.

Nanny, Your Wife Won't Be Back Tonight 303

The First Night 304

— Zhi

The city, the city at night, the dazzling lights shining everywhere, the brilliance of the dance hall entrance attracting the idle and happy people. Gentlemen and young masters, in groups, jump into the dark hall to enjoy themselves, to revel in the air filled with melodious music, the atmosphere filled with women's laughter. They revel, they enjoy, they forget all the world's troubles.

Accustomed to the luxurious life of the city, accustomed to seeing these things, gentlemen and young masters see it as a den of extravagance, but I am already tired of it, disgusted by it. Yet there are still some people, people who haven't entered the den, who want to enter in groups, envying others living this kind of life. Ah, the city, the city is a city that devours people's warmth and blood, chewing on people's skeletons! Those who are infatuated continue to be infatuated, those who are declining continue to decline, but behind them, groups of these infatuated chasers enter, everything is revolving.

Tonight, the wind on the road is exceptionally fierce. It is almost twelve o'clock. Several people, several young people who have already declined, are running on the silent winter night road, shaking their thin coats.

"Thirty days, a full thirty days without coming, it really feels like a different sentiment, doesn't it, old brother!"

The Annamese patrolman on Avenue Joffre stands lonely at the crossroads, his black teeth moving in his cold lips. On the road, that straight line of lights is shaking, and several dark shadows are moving quickly there. Indeed, in previous late nights, whether it was winter or summer, running on this road gave me only an ordinary feeling, but after a full thirty days of not seeing it, a full thirty days of being suffocated in that dim place, tonight, especially on such a calm late night, there is really a fresh feeling, especially since we are going to that place of intoxication.

On the road, the silent road, the wind is blowing, and the dark hands of demons are stretching in every corner. In the dark corners, there are trembling beggars fighting against the cold. In one or two of those cars, it is also dark, but what is broadcast from inside is the delicate and charming laughter of women. Apart from these two different sounds, there is only the sound of our shoes tapping on the pavement.

"Almost there, right? I really can't take it anymore, the alcohol is rising..."

Wang, immersed in half-drunkenness, seems to be talking to himself, running too strenuously, but as soon as he finished speaking, several people had already entered the realm of dim light, and the sound of music was ringing in their ears.

"You wouldn't think, right? Here tonight, wasn't it still in..."

Just as I settled down and my heart finally felt a moment of comfort, Chang patted my shoulder and said with a smile.

"Ha, maybe so! Life is just like this, the changes from morning to evening are uncertain, thirty days, maybe it's just a dream, tonight..."

Sounds that make people drunk and infatuated are surging on all sides, all the men, women, young, and old, are enjoying themselves in this intoxicating sound, jumping and dancing, wasting every second and moment of time. But I, everything only makes me tired, makes me lonely, every place in the world, I only feel the same weariness. Life, that dark, lonely, and depressing life, for me, only stretches on forever, until the moment when my body can no longer move.

Ballad Singing 306

Chen Ruilin and Mao Jia's Paintings

Yuanchang (1120) 5:00 PM to 6:15 PM

Opening Chapter "Newspaper Selling Girl"

I, a girl, grew up in Spring City. Life is difficult and full of hardships. I run around to find a job. Morning after morning, I sell newspapers, shouting loudly. Who responds at dawn? (Wangping Street) People rush to grab and compete, a chaotic mess. The most annoying are the trivial matters. I must be careful with the newspapers scattered on the ground. I rely on my quick feet to sort them out. I fold them high and low in my arms. The Shenbao and the Xinwenbao. They are popular everywhere and sell well. The Shibao Pictorial has been published for a long time. The scenes are colorful and strange. Last year, the Minbao was first published. Laws must be published to be effective. The Chenbao Children's Daily is loved by many readers. Leisurely education is a refreshing change. The Shishi Xinbao is known for its long history. The coverage is increased and the reporting is accurate. Jingangzuan, published every three days. Yao Dui Jingbao is the founder. The Great Shanghai, has a new editorial team. The interesting stories are critical and profound. (Innumerable) Small newspapers are strange and varied. They are nothing more than aids to conversation after drinking. All day I wander the main roads. My stomach is empty and I can barely afford a meal. As the sun sets, the crowds are dense. There is a shortage as people rush to buy newspapers. I sell them arbitrarily, regardless of the date. It doesn't matter if the old newspapers are sold as news. At night, I go in and out of shops. My delicate voice moves the listeners. Do you want some newspapers to pass the time? The price is five cents, very fair. There are always some frivolous women. They frequently wave me over. I was just beginning to understand love. I spent time with my sweetheart. I want to buy love newspapers. I don't care how expensive they are. Love is inherently empty. I advise everyone to be steadfast. Reading newspapers will help you understand the world. You will learn about current events and understand the situation. It is not right to be caught up in the extravagance.

Zhou Jianhong's Big Red Robe

Sino-Western (1040) 11:45 PM to 12:30 AM

Opening Chapter "Bird Words"

A thinking woman is beside her dressing table. She is sad all day and too lazy to apply makeup. The peacock is gone from the tower, the parakeet has not sent a letter. She often meets guests on the phoenix pond, the faithless bluebird is not right. The cuckoo is always weighing in her belly, the fledgling is about to leave its mother's womb. The white-bearded elder on the hall cannot be deceived, the ten sisters know she is faking. At night, tears wet the mandarin duck pillow, the goldfinch is annoyed and cannot let it go. The crow cries with a broken heart, the wild goose cries sadly. She burns incense to the emperor early in the morning, suddenly a magpie brings good news. The oriole gentleman draws near, the waxwing kisses her hand. I am stuck and cannot escape for the roc is tired, the pigeon cannot fly out of her body. Today the birds are going to burn incense. It is as if a parrot escaping from its chains. I hope you can revive the old days of romance. Let the white crane skirt loose. A bow is a slight smile, the kingfisher scolds her shyly. I am a hesitant cuckoo, you poisonous guy don't be silly. I want the mandarin duck to leave quickly.

Chinese Studies 308

Ms. Wang Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Palace Poem by Bai Juyi

Tears exhausted the silk handkerchief, unable to dream,

Late at night, in the front hall, the singing continues.

Beauty fades with age, favor ends first,

Leaning wearily against the fragrant brazier, sitting until dawn.

Presented to My Wife by Zhang You

Moonlight marks pass through the palace trees by the forbidden gate,

Her charming eyes only watch the roosting egret's nest.

Slanting the jade hairpin beside the lamplight,

Prying open the red flames to save the flying moth.

Spirit Gathering Terrace Part One by Zhang You

Sunlight slants and shines on the Spirit Gathering Terrace,

Red trees and flowers welcome the morning dew.

Last night, I received a new title at the top,

Tai Zhen enters the curtain with a smile.

Part Two

Lady Guo received the favor of the Lord,

Riding into the palace gate in the early morning.

Yet she disdains the rouge and powder staining her face,

And lightly sweeps her moth eyebrows to face the Supreme.

Written at Jinling Ferry by Zhang You

The Jinling Ferry has a small building on a hill,

A night's lodging can cause a traveler sorrow.

Palace Poem by Zhu Qingyu

The flower season comes, and the courtyard gate is silently closed,

Beauties stand side by side on the jade veranda.

Wanting to speak of the affairs of the palace with affection,

The parrot in front does not dare to speak.

Radio News 309

The Xinhua Opera Company, founded by Mr. Jin Peiyu, has been in operation for half a year since its first performance. Now, because the company's chief conductor, Mr. Yan Hua, has completely arranged various new programs, it is scheduled to perform for the second time at the Jincheng Grand Theater for five days starting from January 12, 24th year. Film star Ms. Wang Renmei will also make a guest appearance. From the 27th to the 31st of this month (for a total of five days), a special performance program will be broadcasted on the Dunben Radio Station (800) from 5:00 PM to 6:00 PM. In addition to the company's members Yan Hua, Zhou Xuan, Yan Fei, Xu Jian, Yu Hua, Ye Ying, Lin Ying, Ye Hong, Gu Yan, etc., film star Ms. Yuan Meiyun, Peking opera star Ms. Tong Yuejuan, and Yizhi Society members Ms. Chen Jingfang, Jiang Manli, and Yu Jing will also sing. Due to the expected crowds, it is said that spectators will not be admitted.
